et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows how to do it, then one should treat the abscesses long and wide apart.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you sense pain, if you sense tightness.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and if it is for the vein, then look for nearby appearances.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is foolish to cover this abscess, and immediately when it is outside the arms and legs and neck and many other parts, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, the treatment of iron is necessary, and the one at the top should also be covered, and in the one that is inflamed by an artery piercing through the long skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then make a cut in the belly with needles, and then remove the artery of the webs, until it is discovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then push out the other arrow, and pierce it through to the other side, and hold the artery with a double thread of linen, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then do not remove the limb that is between the two ligaments of an intromission until the pus that is in it has been drained.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then administer the care that was prescribed, until the wound heals.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat this inflammation that comes from it, until it is cured.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is in the belly, it is necessary that you clean your hand with what you can from the abscess on all the skin, then pull out the needle outside of the body that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and if there is a double thread, so that you can pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or with one of two threads from the two ends of the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will not hold, then bring another needle to the end of all the thread outside of the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four knots;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then drain the abscess until the excess pus is removed, then clean the wound and leave what is connected.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil, then treat the wounds with bandages and ointments until they are healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come to the artery and vein, abscesses also come to the neck when it is cut, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And there are often complications and doubts in all cases where there are joints, and this is the most common abscess, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it is in many positions with pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is squeezed, the patient feels great pain, and it is not in front of the flesh, but outside the wound.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and moves well from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor dislocate or displace, and that which is in the joints should not be covered by iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance I may have contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and that which is at the neck or face, makes the skin soft:
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, if it has pus, and it is in its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, then suspend it at the tip, and scrape, then remove the bone, and stitch the wound together at the seam, and the treatment until it is healed:
des grosses boces pendans	large jaws hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	No time ever occurs in the belly and no other place, and it is a disease called "funge" by the resemblance of snakes, and it is to the fine roots, and the large joints;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and in it are small and very large;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw the man who had two bellies which were more like snakes than any other thing, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and they were torn, and in them flowed moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I took them and found in one eighteen ounces heavy, and in the other six ounces, and the workings in the incision are such that you look to see if the snakes are moist, and the color of the artifact is white and moist and of fine roots;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If the copper is too wide at the tip, and the fire cauterizer is present.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For in cutting, there often come great bleeding of blood, and if you do not stop it, then hurry to use the cauterizer.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	And if you see the pain spreading and causing fear of the incision of the iron, then take a well-made thread, and tie it around the limb as we have said, and leave it for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	And then restrain, and do not cease to tighten the thread around the limb until it copes with the limb, and work through it.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, then it is necessary to cut them immediately for the belly, but you must also cover half of it, then cauterize so it does not regrow.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then treat the wound, and make sure you do not cover the thalus which is of pale color and poor sensation and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these abscesses are infected, and I will come to the treatment of pus afterward.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is deep
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	if the appearance of the abscess comes from fire wound or cut of a boil, and is above the belly and in some of the bruises, as it has in other wounds, or of blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or of moisture;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is by the bursting of the pustule and by the outflow of pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of blood, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various sources.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is most diverse, and when one presses it to its two sides so it returns, and then it comes back, and perhaps if it is torn, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, do not strain too much.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to blood, it is open with these signs, the abscesses are large and hard, and it is closed according to an amount.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to windiness, then it is frothy at the touch, and the work is that you look to see if it is from the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if it appears to be for the intestines or the bladder, then you must command the patient to stain his linen, and be completely extended straight, then sign all around the belly;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the limb that you have signed all over, then extend half of the abscess above all the large joint;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind him tightly with a strong thread or a firm silk cord, and let him be completely wrapped;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then operate on half of the abscess extended over the limb, and insert your finger, and search for the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you suspect the shoulder is dislocated, and it is, then push it back into place, and push the intestines up from behind the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you suspect the shoulder is dislocated, take it by the bone, and remove any excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery opposes you, or the vein, then go around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two pieces of thread, and push the two needles around what you have done in order to pierce.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it heals, and kill the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	when you see it going underneath and protruding, then treat it as necessary, and drain the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the arrow or the moisture that you have removed, then treat the limb as necessary, and soak the limb.
dou chancre	For the fire cauterization,
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	we have said in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one should treat it with medicines, and how one must avoid the treatment of iron.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and let us say that the chancre enters into the marsh, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when chancres are in a place where one can remove it as with chancre that is in the mammaries, and in the chest, and similar places, and all of it must be removed when it is in the beginning.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	And when it is large and old, it does not matter that you approach it, for I have never seen any heal;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	nor have I ever seen any heal before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the workings, when it is in its place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you remove any once the black bile of the body;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make it heal if it has obvious overfilling, then remove the pain from the good place to do the work;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then pour out your boils or sores, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and cleanse the wound well with your hand or any other thing, and if the bleeding does not stop despite the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding is stopped.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply other remedies until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of hydrocephalus
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	we have said in the division of the resemblances of hydropsy, and how the assembly of the sharp is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the treatment by medicines, and that which is cured by fire.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only illuminated.
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	And one should not touch iron in these two similarities:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	That is to say, tympanites and hypospadias, for it is a fatal matter;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore, when you treat this resemblance of hydropsy which is called "eclytes" of medicines, and the cure does not work, look if the pains are weak, or if he has another disease than hydropsy, as all and solution of the belly and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if not touch iron, for it has doubt.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the pain of great virtue, and he has no other disease than hydropsy only, and he is not too thin nor too old, then thus one should proceed:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Hold the painful area straight above your hands, and the assistants press the abdomen by placing the sharp edge of the spoon at the lowest part of the belly, then take the spinous spatula in this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	and the point should not be too sharp so that it does not pierce the intestines when inserted, and it cannot be bent.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	Then look to see if there is any hernia towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	If necessary, you should make an incision of three fingers' width from the belly button downwards.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	And if there is a hernia due to the disease of the liver, then your incision should be on the left side of the belly button three fingers' width.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	If it is for the mucous membrane, then it should be to the right, and it does not matter that the hairs grow above the wound where the excess does not run to the weak limb.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	Then pierce all the skin with the tool, and push it through, and lift your hand to all the space between the skin and the flesh as if scraping at the quantity of one angle or inside.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then pierce the flesh until the space between the skin and the flesh reaches the desired depth, and this is the length of the blade, then remove it, and push this tool through this form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and is made of light rain or chalk, and has a small opening at one end.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and has three small openings on its side.
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on the other side, and one on the other.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is shaped like a quill, and its form is like the incision that the scribe makes to cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	At the top of it is the hollow, so that when the ink comes to the tip, then you should now place the instrument inside.
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	Empty the other third part, for if you empty it more than necessary at that hour, then by chance the pains may kill him from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he may lose his hand, or he may approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the evil mean, and its hairs.
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then take the instrument and hold the needle, and it is now held by the one who stops the purulent matter that is above the tumor, as I have spoken about, that you pierce in this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then begin the instrument again the next day, if you see the evil suffering, and take from the needle a small quantity.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this every day, and guard against following too much until it does not delay but a small amount of needle.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt the pain, and leave it for a long time, then the treatment of the sepulture or sand cushion, and with much sweat or bath and in the sun, and if it becomes infected from drinking.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the treatment of desiccate medicines until it is healed, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the arrow, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the staff
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever is born who does not have a cord in the staff, or the cord is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to prick often with a very thin needle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put or plug a small piece of cloth underneath, and tie it and keep it in this way for three days or four, and when he wants to make urine, if the cloth is removed, and he makes urine, and then put it back.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	And by chance, it is not suitable, because the urine that comes out does not allow it to be closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is punctured is small, then treat it with a thin silk thread as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who have not the phallus in their shoulder are impotent, because no one is born with a phallus at the top of their back, which prevents them from urinating before it leaves their back.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	And they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come just to the tip, and this is a very bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the way of the work is such that the hairs grow on top of their back, and the phallus and the penis are like the tip of a feather, so that the phallus pierces in the middle, as it should.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and protect from the separation of blood which often happens, and if it does, if the stench of blood which comes from blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the staff
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	often come these abscesses in the thigh, and it is an appearance of a bad wound;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are malicious and not malicious;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	if it is necessary that you incise them at the thin skin, and cut and clean all, then put above cotton moistened in Egyptian oil;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of wounds continues until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if it is a bad dislocation, with a putrid color and smell, then you must apply the fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cleaned it, and if the splinter is in the back, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the splinter that is inside first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when it is removed, then the one outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat them together, do not be sure that the splinter of the bone is not broken, and it becomes black and corruption in its bone and where it is connected.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cover all that is black and corrupted with honey and flour paste made of ground pomegranate seeds and rice, then treat the other wounds until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood comes out, then apply the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	1. The fire cautery is helpful for two positions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	2. that is to say, at the extraction of arrows, and at the decay;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	3. and if the patient is corrupted and withdrawn, then it is necessary that you beat or conduct a lead rod through the wounds, and urinate on them;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	4. and when the flesh is erupted at the end of the rod that has been to those who have not yet been circumcised, or it has for a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scorch it with the instrument cheveit, until the sinews are loosened, and deliver the patient from all parts of the rod;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	If it is a difficult thing to divide the vein, then you must burn it with a small amount of heat from the tip of the knife and the scalpel.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then thoroughly dry between two, and place a thin layer of linen moistened with cold water on it, so that it does not stick.
de la circoncision	For circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not different from other wounds in terms of continuity.
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Therefore, when we perform this work of our will, and especially with children, it is a matter that we should do the best work, and the lightest in terms of health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not direct circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	Because I have seen the greatest part of masters and wise men who performed circumcision in the past, and with force, and all at once.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if there were two curtains, because it has two layers, and if by chance one is lifted up and the other delayed below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	and it returns covered, and the pain is doubled, and to the wound which is from the top is not always assured at the tip of the member.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and to the wound of the finger by chance the iron escapes, and the work is ruined, and often they are born in such a way that they have no need of healing, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the wound healing which is done by force to all the length of the thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut evenly throughout the entire length;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread be well stitched around the skin.
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	And the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if he listens, that you are only binding the thread around the rod as much as possible, and then throw it in all the ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Then place the child straight between your hands, and bring the forces between your hands or away from your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then close your hand around the rod and blow gently, and pull it up until the thread of the rod is tight.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then clean it well of the dirt that is gathered, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it away from one end to the other.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and the second joint of the second finger should be treated with the second herb and the correct index, and balance between the two joints, then lift the hand gently and take the head of the staff;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow slowly and slowly, for this is the most dangerous;
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on and on the powder a piece of cloth glued with the marrow of a well-cooked egg, tempered with rosewater, confected with rose oil and fresh, and let it stay on the other side, and the cure of the other cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the forces at the purification is thus:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The two forces should be equal and sharp, and the forces should also be as great as the hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of the purification is that it is when the knife is inserted into the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Therefore, you must extend it to your angle, as well as when the legs make abscesses;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	And the coping equally, and if you cannot hold it at your angle, then hold it with nails, and then the coping.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they pass three hours, and what is outside the rod is inflamed, let it remain until the abscesses are healed, and scrape lightly;
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If you move the copper as you can move it, and keep away from the part of the rod, it will not harm you.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Therefore, cure the limb of things that are dirty wounds of powder, which we have said or treated for powders, and if you copper too much care, it will not harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure the wounds as we have said, until they are healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is of obstruction of stone, or of blood frozen, or of bowels, or of charred, or of similar things, which we have said in the section.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if his urine is not released, and you see it is retained by the stone that is in the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary to bend the hairs over his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and the feet are placed on his back, and he extends his belly from the upper part of the back, and restrains the hairs as much as possible.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and therefore the neck of the bladder is pressed against the stone from above, so that the urine is released and;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the hairs cause great pain, then it is necessary to administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe", of which this is the form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	And it should be of thin silver wire, as like a quill of an eagle;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and it should be the tail of a long and half-palm, and thin at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie the head of the wool or cotton bag to the head of the thread, and pull the head of the thread inside the catheter;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and fold the excess of the wool and pull it to the head of the catheter, then oil the catheter with oil or butter and egg white, and place the patient on the seat, and the urethra and the clyster of moist oil and olive oil and vinegar;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then lightly insert the syringe into the shaft, until it reaches the base of the shaft, then double the shaft upwards towards the bone.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then press the syringe forward just short of the bladder, and feel the hairs coming towards the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless because the guide or it goes is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then stretch the thread along the entire length of the yarn bit by bit, and the urine follows the yarn, then remove it far, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And restart the syringe until the bladder is empty, and align the hairs.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When skin or blood comes into the bladder, and there is putrefaction and assembly, and you see distillation of waters and medicines, then do all the instrument that is called «clepsedre», and it is the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and has three tubes:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	One on one side, and one on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	And the joint is opened by the doctor's knife in such a way that it does not damage the bone too much, so that if possible, the moisture can be drawn out and replaced as needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	And when you see your remedies going into the bladder, put the tip of the catheter in the moisture, and draw it out through the opening which is there.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you draw the moisture through the catheter, then strongly replace the catheter again.
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	If the moisture enters again, it will come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel the pain.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle plaster with which one applies a catheter to the bladder:
si est ci:	if it is like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	and it is of silver or of lead, and it is the highest of the following:
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and it is disinfected with salt or with lime where the legs are bent.
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you see used to apply a catheter to the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a double thread of strong wool, and heat the poultice above the fire.
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then push the head of the plaster into the rod, then hold your hand over the bladder evenly with all the moisture, until the hairs feel that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	If you do not have a wad of cloth, take a piece of parchment and make a circle with it, and pierce it roundly around.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	Then stuff the thread tightly into these holes, then gather the circle as one would gather a bag, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it with the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And do as you did with the wad of cloth, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the wad.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said in the previous section the ways of arrows and extraction together with remedies.
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	And I have said the difference between an arrow pierced in rain and all signs, and in which arrow one should make a cut.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone that is lodged in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and it is a sign that the sharp blow of the bladder resembles a sharp blow in its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it has a harsh sound, and great pain in the penis, and it can often occur, and then disappears.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and from many of these blows, the foundations;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and it is light in the healing of children until they are four years old, and it is very painful in elderly people, and it is common among those who are between youth and old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	And it is the lighter care of those who have large stones, than of those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with chalk, to draw out all the impurities that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never obstructs one from seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the misaligned joint by the feet, and make it stand up and move away from the center, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and never once rise above the body.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then let him sit between your hands, and his hands be away from his thighs, so that the bladder is completely tilted downwards.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then grasp and touch inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if she does not chop at the touchier too, then grind your right index finger of your right hand with oil, if the hairs are short, or your middle finger, if the hairs are long;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and press at its base, and cut into the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then apply the ointment to the anus;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press above your finger, and cut at the place where you saw it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the minister to press the anus with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand to hold the testicles high, and his left hand to remove the skin which is outside the testicles in the part where the cut is made;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	then place the spatula underneath, which is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	and make an incision between what is between the ribs and the foundation, not in the middle but on the right side of the naval;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and it should be straight above the stone, and your right hand should be at the foundation, and the incision should be across so that it is wide on the outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	if the pressure from the hand that is at the foundation causes it to slip out of place;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and scrape away any stone or edges and margins;
si est griés a issir;	if it is gray to pull out;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is a thorn that is smooth and sharp, like a needle, and round, of which the extraction is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	In this case where it has angles and margins, make the incision wider;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not jump, then you must hold the forceps that are also like a lime at the head, to prevent the stone from escaping;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you push out of the way the instrument sharply curved at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot grasp it thus, then enlarge the small opening, and if there is no skin, then strain it with vinegar;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And if there are more than one arrow, first remove the largest one from the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it should be made larger, and a larger wound should be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the dislocated joint:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or it dies, or the urine comes out through the opening where the bones cannot be set.
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but you must forcefully pull or tear it with pliers, until you remove it in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, bind it, and place above the moilliet cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and vinegar and cold vinegar, to relieve the pustule.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then resolve the misalignment on its own collar, and do not dislocate it from its joint again.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, rise the joint well with oil and vinegar, then apply ointment of mustard plaster and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if an abscess comes into the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and is retained by it so that the urine is held back, which is known in some way as without a leak with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	then place your finger in the wound, and extract that blood clot, because if it remains, it will corrode the bladder, and rot it;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift the wound of sharp and swift and of silk, and help it in all ways that you can, until it is healed;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And it is necessary that all the bandages you use to treat it, that you tie both thighs together, and place the medicines above the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is conducted with a catheter, and tied off, and the urine cannot flow out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if the treatment I mentioned earlier, that you cut many times, is excused by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have experienced this before.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form and be at three angles tied in one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and tie it around the catheter outside the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then push the thread into the catheter lightly, until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and slowly turn the forehead against the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side.
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	if soon comes the urine, then press your hand above the stone that is remaining inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is already broken, and shoots out with the urine, and is sharp against the hairs;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this for any reason that defends it, then tie a thread below the stone and another above, then make the urethra in the place between the two threads, then extract the thread, and release the other, and clean the clotted blood that is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the care as long as they are healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	There is often a need to pierce in women, and if it happens even once, it is the care of the doctor, and it is forbidden for three reasons:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	The first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-versed in such matters, specifically when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third reason is that perhaps one cannot find a woman who is well-versed in this art of hands.
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	And the fourth reason is that if the woman's piercing is more forward than the man's, because it should be made with a deeper incision and great fear is involved. And if necessary, one must send to the surgeon, so it is necessary to have a skilled person, and if you do not have one, do not attempt to perform the operation yourself;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and present a skilled woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command that she do what you command of the investigation of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very carefully if the woman is virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to put her foot or base and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, then hold her away from her base, and recommend that she put her foot or with the painful spot, and press and grind her right hand firmly on the anus.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	if she finds it, then it is necessary to move it from great to great from the entrance of the anus until it reaches the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh, against the middle down, where it is painful and feels the arrow in that part.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move the arm above the stone or below, and let the cut be small at first.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then push the arrow into the wound, if you feel the arrow so sharp that the arrow can come out, and there are many ways of arrows.
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	it is to know, small and large, sharp and blunt, long and round, and those with barbs.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if you cannot pull it out, then put the arrow in vinegar, and hold it for an hour until the arrow is clean.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is fully removed, and have the tools that I mentioned in the extraction of the stone for men to assist you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if it is not removed, and it is the artery that has been cut, put powder on the wound and bandages and ointments, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest by chance the patient might die.
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound has healed, return to your work, until the stone is formed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	wet gauze is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white sponge, which is outside the court of the teeth, which contains the wound.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	And it is called "syphac", and it is never properly in the web of the eye, if one considers that it is from the other eye.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	And it is the thick skin between the white of the eye that we have said.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	And it does not heal on its own.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is weakness that comes to bones, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And if it comes from impact on the eyelids, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	Or it is a changing color from yellow to green, or without red, or black, or watery white, and there are more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to know this condition, because if it is white syphac that we have said, then the abscesses are present, and not long like the figure of an eye, and does not open the eyelids, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the own cloth, then abscesses are treated with a part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought to be another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the fingers and the white sap, then it feels good.
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	Therefore, when you see the color of the moisture, then test all the intermediary parts, from which it was previously formed.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introducer, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cure them with iron, then it is necessary that the hairs be cleaned according to as much power and the replenishment of their bodies.
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	Then the patient lies on his back, on one thing a little high, and puts much cloth on him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then lean over their right shoulder, and command the assistant to hold them on the left, and extend the staff against one of the two ribs near the sternum;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula and cover the skin of the ribs with it from the long bone to above the knuckle, and make your cut straight across the skin of the ribs just below the white line, and carefully scrape the subcutaneous tissue;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	then pierce the white line flat with a sharp needle at a wide opening, and extract all the sharp pieces, and then put your needles, and stretch the white line above;
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the bones of the ribs, but only the sinew.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	and cut out or even piece by piece the costal part of him subtly, for if you do not cut it properly, it will return to him sharply.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the joint springs up at your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the sinew.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then gather the two books of the ribs at one seam, then treat it as with other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	and if the joint is corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, in doubt of the evacuation of blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then apply the bandage to all the suspensory ligaments, and extract the arrow, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if it is sharp and assembled in two parts together, these are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	then apply the bandage to the other part as you have done the first evenly, then suck out the blood, and put in the wound linen soaked in red oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put on another linen soaked in wine and oil, and put over the two bandages, and put on doubled cloths, and tie it over all the limb that is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths and place them according to this resemblance, and assemble them by sewing in the neck of the breeches, and one of them should be placed above the buttocks just at the back, and the other at the part of the elbow;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two should be placed above the two knees, and the entire assembly should be tied in a loop at the belt of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and this branch of the fire cauterization should never be applied in the form of an iron needle, and it is that you should prick the skin with a fine cautery needle, and scrape the skin of the wounds, and heat it as we have said, so that the white scab containing the acid is removed;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Take the fire cautery in this form, and pierce the gum at the teeth, and scrape the skin with this delicate cautery thoroughly.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And the copper in all ways that you can, until you remove everything.
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	And be careful that the fire does not touch the eye.
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	And make sure that this work is safer.
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And keep from the correction of blood, and make sure that the work of tailoring fits well.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if nothing goes against you, or abscess or bleeding of blood or other thing, cure whatever goes against you, according to what is said above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the pain is severe and does not want to endure this work due to its horror, then apply perforation as I have told you, and when you are certain that the acqueous branch is ready, place the painful joint on the elevated seat.
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then pierce the abscess in the outer part with a wide space, and place the perforation far down the body.
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the openings be wide enough that all the sharp pain passes through.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then place cotton on the limb and tie it, and leave it to let the remaining sharp pain pass through, then care for it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	And if the white cloth does not allow the sharp edge to exit from the mouth of the wound, it is necessary that you insert a pen or the instrument used to treat the sharp edges of hydroceles, of which the form was previously mentioned.
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And enlarge the wound slightly, and when the sharp edge returns, and is gathered after six months or within a year, and when it is gathered as before, and thus passes the painful days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	When cutting this branch, many positions cause fear in many people, for which it seems that it is better to leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you the work and similar things about abscesses.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say therefore that many abscesses come from wounds, and simultaneously from the same.
et c’est par mout de cas.	And this is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by excessive sharp and wet, which is spread out in wounds, or from impact.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	And the color of the abscess according to the color of the wound.
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And does not find pain, and is a painful abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And sometimes it is grayish, pale, and yellow in color, and never comes from a vein or an inflammation of blood.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a vein, it is known by the position of the abscess being high, when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	Those who are made of wine grape are known by their arrangement in the expression of the two fingers, and can well make the waist above this resemblance, and above the others.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you copulate the courtesy of the coins, then the eye is in the top, and the tail is of the white swan, and deliver the suspension from all parts of the eye.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the eye is already soiled with these coins, then it is necessary that you take the eye, and the copulation.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is air in the white swan, or in what is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all of that which is held, and the copulation rounded.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the shoulder blade is broken at its base, then it is necessary that you remove it entirely, and extract the bone, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your treatments are completed, apply the wound with soft linen in red oil and wine, then use other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess surrounded by a pus-like envelope resembling a bone, with the softening of the joints, and the painful movement of the limb as it goes.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And the treatment of this disease is as difficult and dangerous as the previous one, and we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	You must make the patient sit with the misaligned joint on the highest seat, then lift the suspensory ligaments of the joints to your fingers, all the tendons that are close to the thigh, and stretch them evenly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then cut the sharp spatula through the wide area of the vessels, until they are exposed, and then scrape each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then I insert a needle or one with double thread, and tie it to the first limb where the vein came out, and tie it to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut them straight in the middle, according to the length of the vessel, and remove the corrupted blood.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then treat the wound as for others or apply a bandage, so that no vessel is cut that would issue from one of the incisions.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	Because by this there does not come any harm, and if it comes to all the veins, then one must draw the cups from all the veins.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	If the person does not lose their strength by the incision of the veins, and they dry out and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The advantages of this chapter are by the section that comes out or syphilitic, or the extension over the belly in the part of the groins, because the intestines descend from that break to one of the veins.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	And this break is either by syphilis, or from the extension of it, and these two ways come from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	from percussion, or from jumping, or from shouting, or from lifting heavy weights, and similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is the extension of the face, that is to say that it happens little by little, in a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal up to the forehead, because the face is close to the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it comes to the section of the tooth, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and has various appearances of abscesses outside the skin, and this is for the outcome of the intestine and the heart due to the tooth.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the worms are found with the intestines, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer from the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cases of iron with fear, for which it is necessary to withdraw.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you command or let the hairs grow on the intestine at its hand inside the wound, if it can be pushed back in;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then place it over its neck between your hands, and lift up the ribs;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then they put the hand above, and cover all the skin of the bones with it.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then push between the buttocks uncinated according to what you have skill to open the wound, and let them be such that the eyes can come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scrape the skin that is outside the bones of the ribs, until the white skin is exposed from all parts.
