et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	And this is the common method of stitching, and it is that you pinch an needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave some space from the edge of the wound, and if it has good thread, sew with a needle.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	And pierce the two needles through the two pieces of leather, which is outside the leather on that side, until you make it pierced from that part, and bring together the two ends of the needle four times.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then the thread of a doubled string around the needle of half a span, then assemble the two parts of the wound evenly, and then leave one span of space, and there make another stitch.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the thread with a doubled string as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you know about needles until the whole wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick, for thin needles cover the whole wound, and too thick ones cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore it is necessary that they be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it does not matter to put the needles too far from the back of the skin and leather, so they do not puncture and open the wound before the stitching.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cover the wounded by the needles, so they do not cause the pain at night, and put bandages or cloths on the wounded by the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of stitching needles is more convenient for small wounds, because it only requires one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second method of stitching is common, and it is that you gather the two pieces of leather and the two pieces of silk together with one needle with a medium-strength thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you have perceived these joints all together, then reset the needle at the part where you began, in the manner that one does with drills.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	And put a space between each stitch the thickness of a thread.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch goes through the man, and I sewed a wound that someone had in his belly, which was cut with a knife, and was the wound more than one inch wide, and it extended into the intestines by two inches, and was the wound inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was dressed with a poultice after 15 hours, and it was treated, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the man had been judged that he would die, and it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not heal it from burning, for I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I placed moss twice a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the two main methods of sewing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and the thread from the part in front just inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the heart of the wound in a straight line, then insert the needle at the top or where you put the thread, and make it pierce from the other side of the part inside just outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the tailor makes the fur, and you leave once the needle of one part, and the repeat of another, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of stitching, which Galen properly calls, is that they assemble the two parts naturally together, and apply one end of the needle to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	fashion a needle or head of the marrow close, and make it pierce that part alone, and leave the two ends of the thread.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from that part before this within, the two ends of the thread.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce both the upper and lower parts of the affected area from below upwards, in two other points called the miracles on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the most common method of sewing and repairing it.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Those who know this saying, and no one testifies to it, you should sew the belly with two needles, or have thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one needle should be inserted from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew lace.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And it is more difficult to sew where the tear is in the belly than other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you clean the fresh wound of all its blood, as soon as the wound has moved, if you reset the intestine and the cost;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on the powder of healing charcoal, and if the wound has moved, then apply any ointment that is present until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and bandage the wound, and let the sage and marjoram be present;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with the others until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	If you do not have any medicine, place it on top of the wound as soon as it begins to bleed, and apply a soft cloth, and shake it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you should not use any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound does not cause communication with the principal members, then it is necessary to apply a light bandage in oil of warm chamomile or rose oil, and place it inside the angles, and remove it from the joints;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if it feels pain or burning in the bowels, and often occurs, then enema of black wine and immediately if the burning comes to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For the puncturing of the intestines, and such things as when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is raw, and this is due to the smallness of the veins that are in it, and due to the subtlety of all the body, and its proximity to nerve nature.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the splinter jumps from the wound, and it is put back in place as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and turned black, then you must tie the limb that has turned black, for blood does not come, as there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut open the belly that is between the limbs, and put the two pins hanging from the part away from the wound, to align the extraction when the splinter breaks, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the breakage of the pot
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the internal organ is pierced, and the wound is small, if it can be put back into some people, because I saw that some men were impaled through the belly by a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it was prolapsed and became a fistula, and in this way there was excrement and vomiting;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to subtly treat it until it was healed, and the wound sounded.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it healing, I doubted that there was no evil in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but it remained in better conditions, and changed and hydrated.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they said no experimenters that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he should be tied in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take large needles, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the needle has opened the mouth, if it puts it above the two lips, so that it holds its mouth above.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cover the needle, and hold it so that it cannot slip, then put the other needle after in such a manner as before, until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	and treat the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the arrow pierces into the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, and it can be tied with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the tip of this intestinal thread that is very sharp, and then tie it to the tip of this thread with a thin silk thread, then pull the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it back into the wound;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of sewing is not far from the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the internal organs, there is no treatment or health, because of its subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	all wounds or abscesses, when they are covered, are universally called "fistulas," and specifically when they are cut and opened up.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is along the spine, a hard and white sore, where there is no pain, and it is as sharp as the quill of an owl;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and never in a clear archway, and sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	never too little, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no scar, it is only because of one of the EIGHT causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
ou por sa malice;	or for its evil;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard charcoal inside, and on the lips, which does not allow fire to come out;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or it has too much blood.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the bones are broken, and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the cure.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is like a plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is late in digestion, and late in health, and blown away by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	when there are openings or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicines in that section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of fistulas that are made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Fistulas can occur in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the face, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the costes, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes from the principal property of the member, and similar limbs.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all wounds of this kind are of great suffering, and there is only labor and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is no wound that does not come immediately to the place that I have said, and you are confident of the cure, and you know how to do it, then take a tent of tin or iron, if the wound is straight, if it is crooked.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the wound is twisted, then circle it with a thin tent of cloth, because the cloths bend around the twist.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the wound is perforated and you cannot well encircle it with tents, then cauterize one of the perforations, because the moisture goes from one perforation to another, and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then carefully examine your patient, whether there is bone or tendon, and if it is broken in two pieces, and ask well of the patient about the pain he feels when you press on his hand, and where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you know truly where the bone is, and if it is far from joint, or tendon, or artery, or vein, or in any of the limbs that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the fractured piece and the corrupted parts that are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deeply in the right place, then you must cut across, as much as you can, then put soft sponges in medicine ague, and press them against the mouth of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous matter that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I apply a warm, clean cloth to the wound until it is clean.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not clean by this method, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the sinus, then drill it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves are not injured or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape away the corruption until it is all bone, then apply a warm, clean cloth to the wound until it is clean.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not clean, and remains red as before, then be careful not to go too far with the treatment:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If you discover and wish to be at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, seek that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot proceed;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other means than to wait for nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pincers, if the instrument is suitable for that, and if there are many bones, then remove them all, do not leave any behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	And if the moisture makes it opposite, and there is no error or fear, then heat and moisture and char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place a warm poultice on the wound to reduce inflammation, and leave it until the flesh is softened around the bones, and then they will be more easily removed.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if they are large bones, such as a leg or thigh, then cut through the flesh until the entire bone is exposed, then close the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is a large part of the corruption, and it comes to a mass around the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it should be cut off all around the corruption, and then treat it until it is sound.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to the leg and was filled with a large abscess, and there was no cause to open it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the wound healers over-opened it so much that the abscess opened, and they let out a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and there was a lot of pain that everyone was groaning and sweating from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And many doctors and surgeons for more than two years, and there was no knowledge in the art of hands, until I was called, and saw her leg and the medicines with which they were treating it, and what was happening through the pores at great speed.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red the veins of youth, and had the color yellow.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that one was coming against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I therefore hurried, and took from one of the pores until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption was coming into the bone from within.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I thought what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption, but that which I had taken.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to heal the wound with herbs soaked in long time, and could not stick together;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then re-examined, and found the bone as before, and discovered continuous corruption in the bone, and the flesh, and then removed it, and I could not heal the limb;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could only remove as much as a palm of the bone, and treat it to its entirety, then heal it with herbs;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healed and stuck together quickly, but did not want to begin the work again except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurred, but he was completely healed, and born in the place of the bone, a hard char, and was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction at all, neither to the other nor to the coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the tooth is broken in any part of the jaw, it should be treated in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take the root, and strain it at the top of the bone that opens, and command that it not be extended upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another thread of linen thicker than the first thread, and tie it above the bone that is outside the bone, and extend the top, so that you remove the rotten part from the outside, and cover the bone above the jaw where you see it should be, so that it does not become rotten;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a piece of cloth outside the bone to cover the rotten part;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it should be as much silk as one can see and feel the corruption, and be another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the tooth is rotten and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then remove the whole char.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then put the cotton on the other side of the corruption, and the silk from one part to the other, and let the silk be as long as possible near the corruption, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, then copper the corrupted joint, and let the silk be in the bone on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	If its corruption is in the continuation of the second joints, there is no other remedy than to cut.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if its corruption is at the tip of the finger or toe, this is very difficult, but nevertheless it is necessary to inquire about that corruption, how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And cleanse it in all the ways you can, but do not let the vein or nerve make you contrary.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And scour that which the incisor and the silk for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of teeth, and their thickness and thinness, their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And therefore, it is necessary to arrange each similar work's tool.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And the work will show you the tool that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you have a tool according to what it needs.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulders may become dislocated either due to within, or due to lack of.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have treated that corrosion by the cure of medicines, and it does not improve, then it is necessary to cover that member until the place where the corrosion comes, so that the pain escapes by the death, or by the malice, which is greater, due to the lack of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are such that the limb becomes black, so it seems as if it has been burned by fire, and it remains black afterwards, for then comes the corrosion of member upon member, and it takes hold throughout the body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if you have a bite from a poisonous beast, such as scorpions of the sea and snakes, if the corrosion is at the center of the wound, and the copper, and do not give it any space to come near your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	and if it comes near your hand, and the copper is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come near your arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, then place the cup at the elbow.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy other than the amount of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and as soon as the cauterization comes or pain:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, then place the cup after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to pain, then place the cup over all the pain.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up the leg, then place the cup at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the bad one die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And the manner of the copper or the cloth that the limb is bound with is such that you bind it above and below, and extend some ministers on one side, and other ministers on the other side, and you soak the flesh that is between the two limbs to the width of a spatula, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then the copper or cloth, and put a piece of linen from each part, so that the cloth does not touch the healthy limb, and comes to the other injury and abscess and boil;
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if blood comes out when you work, then cauterize the limb firmly, or put some stopping powders on it;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medical practice until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a bandage suitable for its condition, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to the man in the same situation:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he suffered from a blackness that seemed like fire burning, and this corrosion first attacked his right side, spreading throughout the body;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the doctor saw the corrosion, he covered the body with ointment, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and for many days afterward the corrosion returned to his right hand, and it came to me, and I put him on things that were reflected after washing the body, and could not stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wishes that I hold his hand, and I do not want, unless I have hope of repeating the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and he also doubted that if I cut his hand, he would not die, for the virtue of the ointment was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he completely lost hope, and returned to his land, and began to cover his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I did not count on anything further than for others to do something else, if they have the matter at hand.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	An abscess never comes in a thin limb, and it lasts so long that it causes great swelling.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then pierce and puncture, and in its outlet the bowels, and let the joints remain as they were, like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is above is also as thin as the cloth you remove, and does not corrode the bone, nor the nerve, and such diseases are called "sinew" and are not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches the bone from the front, it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin if it is that you cover that skin all around, and at the same time when it is thin, like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not stay in place for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have sworn that the skin does not stick, and the corruption is not yet in full bloom, and the skin is charred, then the cure of the ointment is as follows:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look if the wound is large, and the belly that is in it has a foul odor, then the ointment of Egyptian medicine made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take garlic, oil, and lead, equally, and put to cook in a small pot over the fire until the medicine is red, and thickens as much as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take it according to your need, and make it into a powder and a syrup, and apply it to the chest, and hold the pulse steady.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medicine in for two hours, then expel it by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times until the chest is clean and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And never apply the powder of ash, when this medicine is not present, and you should squeeze ashes from grape vines, and pour boiling water on top, then let it cool, and apply it to the chest, until you see that the chest is clean.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	If the patient cannot bear the pain, neither Egyptian medicine nor the burning powder will help, but rather the mustard plaster or honey poultice with a little laudanum.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	Or you apply the honey and wine poultice, where the honey has the property of healing and cleansing, and the wine makes the wound ferment.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this, and you have confirmed that the wound is healed, then apply the mustard plaster that makes charcoal in it, and it is that you hold a definitive poultice, and they make with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	and you cauterize the wound with some medicines and oil, of which I have spoken about their properties or treating burns;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the pus in the wound is small, and the opening of the wound cannot enter, then enlarge it with a needle a little, and put in an Egyptian tent of oil or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, then cut and leave it alone until the skin or wound can enter, and if the pus that flows is above, then cover or higher than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	When the bone is in place, do not let it become infected with char.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the wound as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bone is at the lowest point where it is, for when the bone is in place, do not let it become infected with char, and if you cannot cover the wound as you see fit, arrange it in such a way:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the wound gently slopes downwards, and leave nothing of the wound.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidative remedies to put on the wound, and place them under the cloth that covers the entire wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then apply a compress to the wound in the place where it is slightly larger than the first, since it is often inflamed and swollen on the other cloth according to the size of the wound, and put it on the wound of the healthy part to align the bowels, and do not remove the large dressing until after several days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And the one that is on the wound of the healthy part often removes to remove the bowel, and checks what comes from the bowel, whether it is poison or a little or enough, or digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	And take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in some way and you see the nature that jumps on the wound of the healthy part, if the breasts have already been raised, and approach the healthy one.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then dislocate it in the morning, or at midday, and when you dislocate the wound, change the dressing, and renew the poultice.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts are not digested well after many hours, force them to stand upright so they do not sag.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if the subtle poisons are cut after long waiting, do not despair of the patient's health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people who delay in applying char to their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if they apply it undigested, a sudden jump of the breast after many hours, so that the breast does not move;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breast is delayed in moving, and is distant, then apply medicines that are moist in substance but dry in virtue, such as poultice definitive, for there is a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take a definitive grip, and make it with red oil, and the bandage of old wine even in substance.
puis le confit et en use;	Then cook and use it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And this very thing is best cooked and thickened when a definitive grip is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and the powder on the honey as it is over the fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And then glue the cloth, and place it on the chest, and never administer aristologue along with long roots of heavenly lily, which is also like flour of times and hundred.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in the use of simple or compound remedies:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them, and make powder from them, and put on top of the honey I have said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the cure is long, and not cured by this cure, then scrape away that the corruption is removed, and make an impression in the bone, or on hard members, or on limbs;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the cure of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that arises from outside the joint of the little finger of the hand, or the toe, or by chance arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it is dislocated, and no care is taken, if an abscess comes, and it is covered and poured with boiling water until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps the whole hand.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And when it comes to the corrosion of the bone, until there is painful putrefaction, and the affected part is very swollen, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not improve, then you must remove all the remaining superfluity of the finger, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is also healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And if the nail is close to the bone and begins to poke, and the wound, it is necessary that you put the raw cautery outside of the nail so that it does not pierce, and bring the remaining char upwards, and cover this char subtly and lightly, and place above the remaining char medicines of fire and corrosives to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the remedy of ointments until they are healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, if it breaks and rots, because as much as the bone corrupts, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the tooth rotting, if it breaks and rots, then apply the remedy until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is fierce, broken, and bleeding, and the patient feels great pain, then you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the gum apart in a crosswise direction, and guard that the cut does not reach the bone beneath, because the pain would be too great.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on top to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a sharp sound from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The ones that give birth in the hands of some men are all charred, and sometimes they have teeth, and sometimes they have a hook, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in any of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those born without any joint do not move, and those born at the joint may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The belly of one who is chubby is lighter in some way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	belly it is at its root of a wide space.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	if you have this copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those who are born or must lie on their backs, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh around the bone roundly to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable silk according to this, then care for it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same things that come together in this way come from birth, or from the wound, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is appropriate that you cover that which is sour, so that they return according to their natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two tents or moist cloths with rose oil, so that they do not stick.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	where you place between two pieces of soft cloth, until the bones are heard, as they should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it comes to either of his two hands with the back of the hand, then apply the bandage as it should be done.
des vils	of the evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large and surrounded by excessive melancholy, which come from many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often occur in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should never administer any purgation of clay, and then the healthy one from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment of iron is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is to remove the rust, and then draw out the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cut is made in this way:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	The first leg of sharp hot heat was very strong, until the large one was not subtly removed, then the leg with the bad joint was stretched down from above the knee to the part below the groin.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in the arm, or in the second or third, of a wide size, then lift and pull out the black blood with your hand, from one to the other, as much as the virtues of the bad joint can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then bind it, and command that he be shaved with a black charcoal.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And then restart the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are empty and the joint is exposed.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The application of this method is as follows:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	If the leg is dislocated, if there is much hair, then put it in a bath, and the leg is heated with hot water until it turns red, and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it at the fire, and then cover the vein long at the top of the thigh, or in the part below the knee;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the bottom, and scrape the vein from every part, until it appears when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one can see it red and black, and when it enters or skin seems to resemble a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then press the ray of dislocation, as long as it is away from the skin, and then one can lift it lightly, then the other joint in the same way for three days.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it to the wrist, as you have done, and one can lift it at another lighter place, as you have done first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then cut another size, or if you have skill for it, then lift it, and one can lift it to the second joint of the finger, then remove it and lift it to the second size.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract it from shoulder to shoulder, as far as it is fully extended, then bind it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot pull and lift it, then insert a needle into the thread strongly doubled, and tie it and pull it, and move away from the other side, and turn your hand from one side to the other, as far as it can be pulled.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And beware that it does not bind, for if it binds, then you cannot pull or lift it, and it will cause harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have treated it completely, put soft cloth soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the care as long as they are healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the joint is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must forcefully untwist it, but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron that covers the joint, if it is curved and does not cut through, then it should not cover the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it is of large curvature, because if it were thin, it would cover the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the vein civil
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is injected into the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance arises in another part than the legs, and this has the property of causing the pus that comes out of the skin, as it comes from within the body, serpents and worms, inject between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if there are signs of the beginning of this wound, such as a very large inflammation in the leg, then the limb changes, and the wound begins to open, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two inches wide, and the cloth, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it is not there, if you wrap the cloth around the cloth, and the cloth;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part, wrap it around, and do not cover it at its root until it is completely out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it off, it will enter into the bone and cause abscess and infection or damage to the limb, and severe illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it is necessary that it be treated carefully and gently at the head, and nothing remains or cuts.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and there is never this vein when it is treated from the length of one palm, or ten, and sometimes it comes to me, which issues from ten palms in length, and when you cut it, it bursts or pierces, and cuts through to the bottom, so that all is inside.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and empty out the matter that is inside, and apply to the patient medicines infused with garlic juice on any day, then treat as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never again to this vein, and especially when it opens at the joint of the finger, or toe, and much blood comes out, and it is difficult to stop;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	then treat as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of verses that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often affects cattle, and is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, going up and down, and is felt well from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it was, and jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by the accumulation of certain humors, such as those that come out and wriggle and worms and ascarids or intestines;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its harm, for as it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the brain, perhaps it enters, and destroys the brain;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this has often happened.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it to cure and draw out, then one cannot do otherwise than when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so it is necessary that you tie the limb above and below a very tightly bound bandage, then cut across and draw it out, and if it turns back into the body, and you do not retrieve it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it consumes oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold it firmly away from it, then cut it off and remove it.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to use the mundificament of corpses of medicines dissolved for the evil humors by poisoning. And if it becomes infected with bad meat, it will cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and then moves from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she revealed to me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and soon after, I saw it rise as high as the shoulder, faster than anything, as if alive when cut from the limb;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain separated from the limb and settled in the shoulder, then after a while it corrupted throughout the body, until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that she had turned around in circles around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I greatly marveled at how it moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease move in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I wanted to move the pain from one limb to another, but I could not, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed, and because that appearance of that constraint of breath.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not reveal themselves according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see how to cure this disease, and the pain feels as we have said, if it opens as we have described, then hold the limb above and below firmly, and then cover it with a cloth until that constraint of breath is relieved.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the limb.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then treat the cause of that constraint of breath, such as foul-smelling pills, and serpent pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their similarities and according to the types of bodies they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The varieties of them are such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and curved, and smooth.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those that have the angle, and of those that have tongues, and of those that have pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And that which penetrates into any member if it penetrates according to the ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Or in a principal member, such as the neck, head, heart, lungs, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it penetrates therefore into any part of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you hereafter appears to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If it is necessary for you to perform the extraction of this arrow, for many die afterwards in various positions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully embedded, remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the skull when the arrow pierces and penetrates the bone, and the facial nerve that is above the skull, is when there is scotomy and sode, and esvertin and roujor ens, and inflammation and roujor of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and by chance it is without force of the nostrils, or of the ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance it is the speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and white matter like pus leaks from the wound, and also boils out like broth of cheese.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then take care of the treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it pierces or enters, is that it is near the right breast, and also feels like it was stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow moves like boils, and also cuts through black blood, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and syncope.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, without doubt, the dead will rise.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a wound that does not heal is that without any pain, bubbles rise from the wound, and the throat swells, and the limb changes color, and it gasps for breath and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the roof, it is below the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and there is great blood and great pain and breathing.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the stomach, by chance if anything of undigested meat jumps from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the belly, and nothing comes out of it through the intestines, there is no hope of cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bladder, and the urine shoots out and comes out afterwards, and the pain is very great.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Therefore, it is a mortal wound.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the hand and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and spine of the back and forearm and wrist and fingers and legs, and similar members, are safe according to many arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to the man that an arrow hit him in the knee at its base:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and it was taken out from another side, away from the ear grease, and it was healed without a trace.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And in a game, there is an arrow that pierces the grease of oil outside the paper outside, and the arrow is recovered, and it can only reach the tip towards the fist, and it is a large arrow of a Turkish bow, all the iron light without ears;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	the game was safe, and no bad accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And in a game, there is an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it is an Arabic arrow with ears;
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I sought the arrows, and subtly I found it, and it was safe for the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I inserted an arrow into a man, which was in his head or stomach, and thought he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and pulled it out, and inserted it again, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you want to a man who has an arrow that has fallen out or back, and the wound is sealed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and remains inside him, and does not change his natural condition, nor find harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you want to another man, who has an arrow that has fallen out into his face, and the wound is sealed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and prolongs thus without great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And a arrow was stuck in the man of the king, which was his neck in the middle, and it was somewhat inclined to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for healing after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I found it all in a very thin tent, and I did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt sharp pain and pain on his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I put above his head a poultice of digestive attractant, because the wounds did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and to me appeared the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I immediately applied the ointment on it, and soothed the wound directly, and waited until the pain subsided for a long time, as he felt the arrowhead inside his nostril.
et il le me dist.	and he told me.
