Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied the corrosive medicine on the wound immediately, as long as it was open, and I tested it, and felt the head of the arrow sticking to the skin.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pushed it into the opening of the wound with that medicine until the head of the arrow appeared clearly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And it passed well the ends within four months, and then ulcerated the wound that I had sown the stitches, and one from one side and the other, and could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore, I continued to subtly and ingeniously manipulate tools, until I took it on the next day with well-made stitches, according to how its form would come at the end of this chapter, as I do, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctor judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and it was healed the wound, and was completely cured of all pain.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, because the books cannot comprehend everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the wise masters know well very little, and what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, for the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not issue from members unless they are pierced for two reasons:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the limb where they enter, or by another part.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which comes out by the way where it enters, is an arrow entering through the muscles, and never comes out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if she does not jump now, let her remain until the charcoal is ready to be placed around it, and also to make an opening for the release.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot be released, let her remain thus for several days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then she jumps, and if she does not jump, pierce all around with a thin needle, until the surrounding tissue is expanded, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the skull bone, and goes towards one of the bellies of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	if not pulled immediately, but left until it is even after some time, because if the arrow comes out too soon, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not embedded only in the bone, and does not come out of the skin, and remains in place without causing any harm for several days, then the method of pulling it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very deeply embedded and cannot be removed, then apply tar as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is placed back in the body but cannot be seen, then cover it with the entire tent.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with any suitable tool.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot pull it out due to the narrowness of the wound, and because the arrow is deeply embedded, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, then leave it until the wound becomes large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and retrieve the arrow if you can, and if it has ears in the arrow that it holds, then break the char that is stuck on two parts to the muscle that you can, and then break or pierce the ears of the arrow, until you can retrieve it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully remove the arrow, so that you do not break the arrow when removing it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, then pull the limb towards the shoulder, as the extraction is alleviated.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if blood flows from the wound, follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and guard the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put care as you can muscle to remove the arrow without danger, or soon or late, or firmly or weakly;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow left, as this is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, where it does not open anything of its own, or where the skin is inflamed in some place so that one can see or feel it apparantly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut across, as much as the needles can take, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, round your hand and push it into the bone, until it enters the bone, and expands the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	and if it cannot come out, then leave it and then restart the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is from an arrow and it is still in, if it is stuck at all;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it is stuck in the flesh, and you see administer gently, if you administer the instrument straight, so that the arrowhead enters the hair of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	then pull out, and if the arrow is stuck, if you pull out the instrument at an angle, to alleviate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	and if the arrow is stuck in the belly or bladder or side, and it is close, and you can cover it over, if you can;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and guard yourself from covering the vein and artery, and then extract it, and then cut into the wound, if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways to do this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Great, medium, and small, depending on the amount of blood.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the beak of a bird, to stick at the point of the arrow, as in this way:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the barbs to hook and to hold is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins common to the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of the veins that are opened, there are 31, of which it has or head 16, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	2 beans that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the 2 arteries that are in the 2 temples appearing.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the 2 veins that are in the 2 arm pits of the 2 eyes, which are called "aspires".
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is located in the forehead
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is located at the back of the head
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two temples that are located on the sides
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are located above the lips, and these are the veins that are called "augerich
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are outside the tongue
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly bled are five in each arm
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and is on the right side, and is called by the common people "vein of the head
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	And the common one is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilar, and they call it the lay people "vein of the heart".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the basilar is on the right side, and they call it the lay people "vein of the belly", and it is above the fossa, and it is that one from which one bleeds, which opens clearly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the subclavian is the vein that is between the brachial and radial, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	And in the leg and where the feet are, there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	The first is outside the pouch of the sinister side rib, and the second one is above the knee of the dexter side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	et the vein which is called «nesse», which is in the elbow of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins above those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The purging of the veins that are after the ears helps with ancient catarrhs, and migraine;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the purger, as I told you, and it is that you reset the head of the pain, and rub the limb where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then strain the pains on its neck to a ligature, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two loops depending from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	where you feel the bone out of your joint, and if you sense the pulsation from your joint, it is dislocated;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and place it outside the vein next to the bone, then lift your hand all around the vein, and cut and scrape the skin and the vein well, so that you can see through it twice;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and tie it until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already mentioned the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples, which is worth avoiding, and sodden, and accustomed to being covered with tears;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of a good surgeon are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and he knows his own neck, so that the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and he feels the hairs on the other's back, and then inspects it;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the skin over the vein at the back of your hand, and pierce it with a lancet from outside, and lift the vein upwards, and tie it off, as you have done in the other two veins, and draw out the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the hairs, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put gauze over it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then the bandage is formed, and it is left until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken about them and their treatment and removal, as the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the facial vein is as valuable as the healing of the cerebral diseases of the face, and migraine, and rheumatism.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the pain is felt in twisting the neck, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosser", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the point on the vein, and hold it firmly with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the neck from its dislocation, and tie the vein until it is healed and never again with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, the fire should not be too hot;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the iron should be straight, because the teeth are close, and by chance it may break the flame when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The use of the two veins that are in the two arms helps with the eyes, and the jaw, and the jawbone, and the cheek, and the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their vein is such that the pain dislocates its neck by twisting from any joint, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then, the healthy one, and let the health pass through the wound, a little long with the flame, a little wide, for there is no hair.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are too delicate, perhaps it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then apply pressure to the blood, as much as you have skill, and then tie with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The health of the vein from the neck is good against fever, and for sweating, and for diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that comes to the face, and always when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the health is such that the pain strains its neck, then strain its neck to your right hand, and take the delicate flame long, and put it under the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the saint will begin to bleed now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not move too much in the meantime, and draw out the blood according to your need, then tie it up for a night, as it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the shape of a flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The sainfoin of the second kind helps to narrow the aloe, and at the beginning of mesmerism, and for many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosions, and herpes, and stomatitis;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the sainfoin is such that the diseases avoid its neck from one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the masters be above the head of the dislocated part, and the dislocated part below the seat, then gently lift the limb with a long, slightly wide, and then drain the blood frequently, as much as necessary for the matter.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then repeat on the other vein, then release the limb, and hold the veins steady, so that the dislocated part does not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it rest until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the lips above helps in the mouth, and in the corruption of teeth, and fissures of lips, and soreness and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the healing is to make the dislocated part sit in front of you, and hold its neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the eyelid, and look at the two veins, one on the right eyelid and the other on the left, which are known by their black color and by the small black veins around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Then cut both of them, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, cut the largest one from each part, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the tongue's disease
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The veins that are below the tongue help after the sainie of the cephalic, and it is at the narrowness of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of a good physician are that the hairs between your hands before the sun, and the tongue is relieved, and look down each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	therefore healthy both and not move too far away, for from there are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins that are commonly cured are cured in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pressing all the fire wide, or by oil-like, as if cutting through, and is called "anesel";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fire cautery is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open veins that have been sewn closed with thick blood that is clotted and disturbed;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of a flaming torch:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more delicate and pointed, and is for opening veins that are delicate, where there is delicate clotted blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and where the collarbone, and where the shoulder, and where the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the vein to be opened carefully, and that it be separated from the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and blood clots come out, then it is necessary to cool it as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and it should not be pricking the fire, but cutting as with a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilisk does not open clearly, then it is necessary to restrain and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want any blood from it, or you clean in its place the vein with your arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the copper to the fire as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see that you know the vein of the sinew, then it is necessary to restrain the arm and touch the vein until you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then signal the elbow, and then tie the arm, and cover the wound with a flame afterward.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and watch that you do not pierce into the artery when you see the elbow swell, for it is the artery.
eschui la donques.	then move away from it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it spouting out as high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, then it is not from the artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	then quickly move away from it, and put your finger on the length of it, then remove your finger when it is not stained, as it often does.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	tie the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the hairs;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is fear, do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	and if the pain is not alleviated, and it hurts, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, for the main part of the remedy is to stop the bleeding;
et estainche li sans.	and relieve the pain.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of cloth, and cut it, and take one part and tie it well to the other side;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the pain is relieved, that is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then the doctor, as we have said, applies powders that stop bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stoppage is not always effective in many positions of the small wound of the limb, and the position of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The cleaning of the vein in the middle helps because it treats blood from the top and the body, as it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the cleaner to move for the vein that is outside, and if not too far from the front, and he finds the vein, and it swells and the santez is not stopped.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve is often open, and if it does not open in any men due to its subtlety, then you must use the instrument accordingly.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	shield the nerve from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has veins between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The remedy for the cerebral headache helps, that it draws blood from the head, and helps with the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is recommended to use the remedy by applying a garlic or mint oil fire, because it is the safest of all veins, as it does not affect any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, it is recommended to use the lighter limb, and do not harm anything if it does not work the first time, and then start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, some men's arms swell to others, but it does not harm them the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you need to know about healing is that healing is only intended for the purpose of maintaining health and preventing diseases from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	And whether the healing is done in one of the three veins that are either open:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	That is to say, cephalic, fasciculic, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And it should be healed at the beginning of the first hour, and in the afternoon and in the evening after eating, when the sign of repletion appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	And it should be cleansed on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The cleansing that is administered to diseases does not have a determined time, but it is best to do it in the morning or at night, every hour and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not necessary to cleanse children under the age of fourteen, nor a pregnant woman except for the first three months after conception.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Do not let those who have passed sixty years old become physicians.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wants to cleanse, in whatever way it is done, it is necessary that he empty the intestines of a light enema, if he has much feces retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous waste harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Do not trust those who are too fond of meats, nor those who are overfed, so much that they are full of humors;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one becomes ill after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent menstruation, and of living with a woman, and of travel, and of watching and fasting, and all the virtue, or by any other cause of the arm or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly remove the humors, if they are not too thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter or take a bath, if nothing prevents, to subtly remove the blood, and save the vein from the third hour, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself from that day of work, and point, and luxury, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be bound and joyful, and let the physicians be higher than those who heal, and friction the arm II or III times, then restrain the joint above slight movement, for if it is too stiff or weak, it cannot correct itself;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then friction the limb with hands, until the veins swell, and feel them to be full;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then milk the physicians the flame of a small amount of old oil, then place their thumb on the vein nearest to the limb where they want to heal, that the vein does not burst and fail to heal;
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	Because there are veins that flee as quickly as strings to the surgeon, and some that are plain of thinness, so that when one puts above the flame, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if the surgeon opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, because it is necessary that the surgeon be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the first time he opens the vein, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	But if not, he should restart a little below that vein or above carefully, if the vein is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the joint is inflamed, and the pain subsides, leave it for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	by chance it may come abscesses.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter or bathe, then restart the cleaning if it suits him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small, or you rub it gently and doubt that it will not bleed as much as you saw, then trust that wound itself directly to all the fire.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work it gently, if the joint is inflamed.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swelling, do not start again with the same salve, and put on a little oil, for it soothes the blood in the wound, and is better in this limb than the salve.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the oil salve in each wound that you cleanse the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	And this very thing makes a triangle and a bow of the herb, when it is put on the limb.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If subtly draw out the wound and separate it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if some large abscesses come, which often happen, exactly when it is not cleaned except at this time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and put on the limb sponge moist in hot water and a little salt, and hold it an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place for some time without any discoloration or greenish tint, then it is not harmful.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place on top of anything with aloe or mustard mixed with honey, ointment, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there is an abscess and appearance of the pus from the church.
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	and therefore place your hand on top, and if you feel the swelling soft with the pressure of your hand, then it is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore do not place anything that we have said on top, because by chance without the artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but apply a dry bandage to strengthen the joint, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And apply each bleeding according to the amount of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if it is not black, let it remain out until it turns red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it swollen, let it remain out until it becomes thinned.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is suitable for one who is lame and disabled, and has the skill of arrow extraction, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for one who is weak, do the opposite, and let him heal quickly and often, and it should be treated by cutting across, not by pinching.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	This method of healing is safe from the corrosion of blood and the straining of tendons, and it is better than healing by a long or wide wound.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to those who have a bleeding wound, it is appropriate to give bread mush in the juice of green apples.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is hot-blooded, then apply blood three times or four times. And if it is of cold complexion, then before the healing give bread mush in muscat syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and strong-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he has a fever after the evacuation of much blood, it is necessary to give him a broth of meat, and an odorous syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the chapter or section on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to drain some arm and bleed again, it is necessary that when he is weakened by much bleeding, he should do so little by little, according to the quantity of its power continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wishes to drain some arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong pulse, he should bleed again seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And those who wish to heal on another side, they must heal at the second hour or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	Because he has much blood within his body that is already heated, and causes fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to draw a large amount, and widen the vein until it pierces into the flesh.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you should meet all conditions of health, and place your hand on the wound as it heals, so that the patient does not die from bleeding, which has often happened when the healer is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and do not draw when you see the arm weakening, and make blood flow out a second time, and the vein is closed, that you press strongly on.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is curved, he should extend his arm quickly, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let it rest until it heals the second time.
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you do not point to the tip of the flame, until the blood that is frozen from the vein is softened, and put on a cloth soaked in oil, and press it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the pus is seen to be flowing, let it flow and do not press it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood the second time, draw it from the same vein, or another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are sound because they are composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of healing is that the hairs bring their hand in sharp hot, until the pain is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then tie it gently, so that the vein appears well, then heal it across, not too narrow or too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the pores be wide, and clean well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow in the hot water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is already in this state, do not turn the hand again in hot water, for it is put more in ice than in hot water.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the bleeding of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding of the wrist vein on the right side is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and apply hot and sharp, until the vein is punctured, if possible.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the vein is crossed, and if you manage to catch it all at once, without causing any harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And do not move too much in the beginning, for the veins are all over the body, and then put the hand back in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary, if you put oil and thread over the vein to sew quickly, and thus do for each rain.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve for the hand on the right side is good for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you to the left.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve for the breast is good for all diseases that are not of the body, such as diseases of the marsh, and retention of flowers, and disease of the rain, and of the coxes and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its blood is such that the hairs boil in hot water, and rub on the vein until it stops, and tie above the joint.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and if the vein is at the elbow, and from above the wrist there are many raindrops;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then use the larger rain, or at the elbow, which is more suitable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you use it above the wrist, then guard against the nerves that are displaced, and apply it as if in scraping.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be equal.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot issue from the sinew, then reset the knee in the high position, and let the vein fully drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the first application does not work, then start again from above a little, because the veins are salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	and do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus apply the same soporific to the other wrist.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the knee of the thigh, and its sinew is worth the pain of the hip, when it is for an arrow wound.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his health is such that the hairs between or in the bath, and strange above the ankle four times in twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then the healthy one in all ways that you can, and across;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worthwhile to cover it, because the limbs are sore, and it is very painful for men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not relieve it, then the healthy one of any that opens or falls from a piece of cloth, and towards the small toe, and it keeps the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make so much correction of the blood that you see, and then release the ligament, and put on cotton and hold it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of wounds by suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vacuum devices are made of horns, or of brass, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And suction is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this suction without pricking is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Either it is at all heat, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And the suction done by pricking and drawing blood is done in twelve places on the body, of which one is entirely at the top of the chest;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are at the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in the second rib of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction from the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction from the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction from the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suction from the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suction from the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suction from the two knees;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suction does not treat blood, but only the small veins that are scattered in the body, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone, as is done with venipuncture.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered except in cases of extreme heat or cold, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessary for illnesses, it is advisable to ventilate, or by custom, to uncover each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every ten days.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they have the task of ventilating, have heavy heads;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and some who feel pressure and redness in their face, head, and neck, and darkness before their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have extended their tongue, and spit blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and some who faint, and see black spots and pale faces and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is at the end of the month, we command them to fast for three hours after midday.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The saliva of the mouth helps to ease the pain of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it should only be after the evacuation of all the blood from the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this ventilation is in place of the saliva of the head, and it should only be used by those of cold constitution or who have diarrhea, as this does great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason it should not be used by those who are watchful or who have cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves, if they become forgetful, and for this reason, it is necessary to place the vacuum a little lower due to the uncertainty of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation of the neck is in place of the saliva of the head and the basilicon, and because it is good for the narrowing of the throat, and for the opening of the pomegranate, and for all, and for replenishment.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it should not be placed too tightly, for if it is held too firmly, it will cause the spine or stomach and heart to twist.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilation of the second costal cartilage of the neck alleviates head pain, obtunds and eliminates migraines, prevents strangulation, and relieves pain in the roots of the teeth, and is in the place of the health of the basilica;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is necessary to command the healer that he press his hand when placing it, so that he does not compress the artery, and does not cause bleeding of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventilation of the lower jaw relieves mouth disease, and decay of teeth, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the joint of the second lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is for diseases that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The incisions of the shoulders are just as valuable as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And the healer instructs the patient not to fear too much pain, for the bones are bare of flesh, and can be seen through nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The suction cup placed on the back is just as valuable for drawing out morbid matter from the foundation, and for diseases that are not visible, and it should be large and made of metal, so it can effectively draw.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And by chance, if it is too thin, it will break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The bandages of the legs open wounds widely, for they draw out blood from all over the body, and cause ancient pains of rain, and of marsh, and of the bladder, and remove the flowers.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are in the place of the second phalanges, and of the second metatarsals, and always they weaken the body after long use, and cause pain in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to put the bandage is that you first place it empty, and suck quickly, and apply firmly, and move evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the affected part red and swollen, and open the wound of the blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then apply heat, and replace the bandages, and take care of the body's position, for there are some who have sores and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to make a single cut, and it is necessary to make large wounds and deep ones;
et suce legierement.	and clean lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the wound is not large, then it is necessary to make two cuts:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the wound is not very deep, then it is necessary to make the third cut;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out the blood a little and a little, then we should only clean once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, then we recommend often.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is not let out, then we apply heat, and the end is that the wound should be cleaned thoroughly, and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and are tough, and who have hard pores, that you use the legs of the oil suction cups, which are appetizing and dissolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this state, of oil violet, or of almond sweet oil, or of cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the ivy state, of lettuce oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or balm oil, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if that person who is to have a wide and large opening, should not put any oil, but it should be washed after venting with hot rosewater, or hot cold water, or water of elderflower, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from the ashes of silphium, or hot water of mint, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive flesh rise from old wine, or from sour wine, or from the decoction of anise or chamomile, or from other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and they should not immediately apply suction after the bath, but an hour or two afterwards;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and they should not sleep immediately after the suction, and it is good that they warm themselves, when they should be sucked and when they are sucked.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And if those who are suctioned are cold, and if they are not enough and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is good that they take cold things, such as large apples and endives and lettuces at the mouth, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and put on poultices, and bread of mustard, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, take honey syrup, and aromatic wine between old and new, and put on poultices, and poultices of mustard, and moist meats; and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day that he will move around, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is appropriate to give some men ginger or muscat wine before or after movement, to strengthen the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let them subtly give the water, but it is not appropriate for everyone to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The suction cups that are placed to cause pain are those that are placed on the liver, and on the mouse, and podagra, and on the belly and the buttocks and the legs and the thighs, because these members do not suffer pain in those places, and no one does it except to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on the breasts when the baby is born;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to overcome the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the belly and on the buttocks to ease the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is a bone or stone, by its attractive power perhaps removing the bone, or dislodging the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus she does when placed over the liver and over the stomach when there is wind retention, and these vacuums are administered empty for suction only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and never administered together with fire, and sometimes plain hot tea, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the vacuum with hot boiling water, or hot water in which he has cooked poisonous herbs for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the pneumatic administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two large and half-palm-wide openings and is surrounded by a small perforation, just like to put a needle, and if it is of tin, sulfur before so that it does not burn the pain when placing it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and in the middle of it, a rod of iron or wood, to put a splint, and they are both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups of children are different from the old, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should put this suction cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	with a wax splint or linen, and put it in the suction cup at the end of the rod that is in the suction cup, so that it clears both the back and front of the suction cup that it does not burn the hairs.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then place it on the limb, and you should put it on the perforation that we have said, so that when one wants, it goes through the vapor, and one removes the suction.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And grasp the line as before, and restart it often, if you have skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction that is administered in disease of pleurisy, at all acute, does not have a probe or perforation, and is not administered until it is full of acute, and is placed on the limb alone.
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Noses are not administered until in limbs where one cannot place suction for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar ones.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and when removing a horse's shoe, as with two or three nails, and similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is such that when you cut through them without any obstruction, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in fresh water, as long as they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then clean them with blood and a syringe, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the nails on top.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat and ready, if it is possible to put a syringe there, place it, as it is very useful afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the arm gently, first from the shoulder, then from the elbow, very well, and then wipe it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if it is too sore after the course of the sinews, then rub the linen cloth in cold water, and put on it, until the wound is cleansed.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wounds multiply, then put on it broken glass, or salt, and similar things, until it is cleansed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put half of the crushed beans on the arm, and leave them until they dry on the arm, it will stop now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more serious cases, take other remedies.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the remedies do not want to take effect, rub the wound with fresh blood, or you make a needle until it enters the wound, and then place them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will stick.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are biting, powder them with a little aloe and ground silk, or ash, they will now bite.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen, foolish child, that the evil fate may not befall this chapter, that they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor lettered them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the knowledge of this art is lacking in our land, for I have not found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, except by the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that will be brought, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise man places his understanding, and delay over the truth, so that those who are experienced find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or wound comes to any one, it is necessary for you to quickly clean the dirty part on one side and on the other, if nothing stops you, such as weakness of body, or children, or old people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	when he does not hold him tightly or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and uses cold charcoal, that is to say, cooling juices, and oil of eye and of cartilage, and does not drink wine, and does not use any heavy meats, and does not fill himself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of an abscess forming, or spreading of matter to the member;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the pain returns again under his former management that he used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to apply a moistening remedy that causes swelling, such as cooked wheat, and rice, and tests, and beans, and piez, and fish, and wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the moistening remedy may cause pain and more quickly the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and infirm cannot be well put back together or healed according to their nature because of the corruption of the members, nor also those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but do not care, reset it over the broken bone and large thick rods that support and join the limb together, as long as it holds as it did before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not touch it at all in its work, and because it needs to be fed with large amounts of food, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And there are various ways to break bones in many different manners.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the breaking of the shoulder is different from the breaking of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes through the arm, and another in soaking, like the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break all in a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every way it has its intention, and its proper tool in the restoration, according to what memory comes in its joint;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known the breaking of the bone because the joint is twisted, and open widely by default, and its at the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting at the joint, and the limb does not feel great pain, there is no fracture.
