mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can still have twisting, or a wound, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it by hand, but put on the remedies that come after, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And if the fracture that goes through the arm, and both parts are disjointed, then you must now set them evenly, as well as abscesses which come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses come, if you leave no pus, until the abscess is soothed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it evenly in the muscle that you can lightly and safely, and if the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of that which has pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then reset it as it should be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if it is a bone broken into pieces, then reset it in two parts, if it is a hand or foot, or at your hand if it is small members, or at two strings, or at one string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken bone are aligned, then reset all the additions in their places with care that by your work no injury or pain comes.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and well support the two bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And if it feels good to the hand when it seems not to be quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if it is stretched well and not restrained too much, and does not press as those who bring it through their work abscess and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, well restrain the bad that it does not move, neither while awake nor while sleeping, nor while turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard well that the limb is so assured that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not quite in place, and the limb should be placed in proper position so that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and ensure it is set correctly, as twisting can occur when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The qualities of the member broken are different in size and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members, such as bones and fingers and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is appropriate to wrap them in soft and thin linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as the ribs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is appropriate to wrap them in a wide and sturdy bandage, because the large limbs envelop the whole member, and they hold it equally from all parts, so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then lightly lifts the limbs, three or four times according to the limb, and holds the hand a little at every joint, then goes above the fracture and holds it less, than the fracture is gradually moved away.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and gradually softens the limb a little and a little, until you grip a large part of the healthy limb, then take another limb and return around directly above the broken limb.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part away from the fracture, and holds it gently, not too hard or too forcefully, as we have said in the first section above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the limbs wet linen or cloths, until they are evenly aligned, then tie everything together with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is inflammation or an abscess, then place something soothing on top of the abscess, and what removes the inflammation, and leave it like that for some time.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain over your splints, and they should be half of a wide bandage, or of buckskin that is properly cut, or of palm leaves, and they should be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the nail that one puts over the break be a little bigger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and it should also be as long as it needs to be for the limb of small or great size;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then stretched over the nails as you have done in the first layer, then tied with a thread evenly, as in the first layer over the broken part;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is, the less;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it should be that the thread is medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, like what I have seen in the works of those who make laces with linen ropes, and that is great error, because the layer cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should only have between each nail about two finger widths of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are closed by the needles of the stitches after straightening them in their places, put some discharge of linen or other clean cloth, so that it does not become infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splint, and the bandages are broken, I will tell you the treatment later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And it is not necessary to straighten all the broken bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	When the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put stitches immediately, but after five days or seven, or more depending on the safety of preventing an abscess from forming.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and here is the method of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and you take flour that is kept in the walls of the mill, and mix it with an abundance of egg, and use this mixture, which is not too clear or too thick, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring fractures to many positions, and specifically to women and small children, for it is not too hard nor too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way to apply plaster for healing fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take equal parts of beeswax, gum Arabic, resin, and pitch, and boil them together; then add mastic and frankincense, in the same proportion.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Add myrrh and aloe, in the same proportion.
alechil VIIII З.;	Add a little oil of lavender.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	Grind it into a powder and mix it with egg yolk.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it quickly heals broken bones, and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of splinting that is useful for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take a cloth and soak it in cold water, then apply it to the affected area.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Mix equal parts of honey and aloe vera, then apply it to the affected area.
acaice VI З.;	Apply a cold compress to the affected area for six minutes.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Grind ten grams of bole armencian and mix it with either vinegar or an equal amount of egg yolk, then apply it to the affected area.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of splinting for joints and bones that have been dislocated from their sockets, and to relieve the pain, and to support the weight of the bone, and to prevent further breakage.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new cloth, and soak it in oil and cooked lard, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These bandages do not heal immediately, but they are good for easing abscesses and properly treating pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to set broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and earthworms, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat the healing of broken bones and to ease the remaining pain of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take valerian root, chamomile, violet flowers, and flour of each one in equal parts;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is hot, apply the mixture with fresh coriander juice or vinegar, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of applying the plaster more strongly than the first, when an abscess is resistant to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of wormwood, and seeds of linen, balm, melilot, and saffron, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and preserve with vinegar sharp or sweet, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore it, for the reason that a cerote made of wax and oil was used, and nothing else, and he said that it should be between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to restore it, with dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to treat wounds and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mallow and horsehair, or feathers of an owl, and wormwood, and silk equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it to the affected area.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then release it a little later, and be careful if the hairs do not feel any pain, nor has the bone of its joint moved;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if it does not move by itself after that.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, whether at rest or swelling, then hurry, and release it, and apply the dressing now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take light bandage, and wet sponge with salt water, and immerse in hot, and lift the limb, until the itching stops, and ease the pain;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, boil in hot or rose oil, and tie with a bandage, until you are sure of no abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and rest the inflamed member, and relieve the pain, then begin the subtle binding, and a little plaster, and do not strain it too much as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	as gently as it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is filled with pus and redness and pain and swelling, and you have the skill of plastering and bandaging, then treat it evenly as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if the member does not come back to its place as we have said within three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never leave it more than twenty days, according to what we see, until the breaker is healed and approaches the position of the char above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then the strain more than before, and it increases its flesh, as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the limb stiffer than is usual, it is not possible for numbness to come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then apply hot and sharp needles every time you remove it, and this should be done for each day, and release a little the ligament.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	then cut through the numbness in the limb, and change the position of the limb frequently as the foolish ones do, to relieve the pain.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is evil, and this work is not safe, and I see nothing else but fatigue and doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of breaking are, and various shapes, and the causes are distinguished;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	because it has breaks that are made by the percussion of a spear, and the collarbone is completely broken through to the shoulder blade which is outside the bone, as if it were broken or fractured;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and therefore this type of break is called "fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	or the spear pierces the bone from above and penetrates through it, and this type of break is called "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and this is the wound of these two breaks, which are either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion from above, or a cut or from the fall of a stone, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if he has a broken bone that protrudes, which approaches the skin that is outside the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is placed in the bone as delicately as a hair, and the fracture is small, and therefore this break is called "hairline";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound that is made by being struck with an arrow, or falling, or by something similar, and allows the piece of bone to enter, and is fixed in place like the cauldron when it is placed on the cauldrons.
si entre li piere dedens.	if the arrow enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And there is more to those who have or wet bones, like that of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and they have in all these ways of breaking that small pieces are removed as these.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of fractures by the withdrawal above them, and inquiry with tenting, and by the corrupted flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known because when the bone is exposed and rubbed with something, if there is an open fracture, it is black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, beware of bad accidents, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes coming out and reddening, and other similar things in many conditions, it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any obvious injury, and you hope for healing, then begin treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the broken bone comes first to you, and it is in the leg, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day, so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the arm, then you must remove the bone before the seventh day, provided that the skin around the bone is not decayed, and the injuries that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the cloth that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you cut the broken part in this way:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and that you hold the head of the painful joint, and uncover it over the bone in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound as softly as you can, and if blood comes out when opening the bone, or an abscess forms, help it with what is necessary, and that you fill the joint with cloths moistened in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and be sure of the opening of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove around the bone, and it is done according to the two ways of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	The one way is that you copy the narrow cut in front of it, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second way is that you have many different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And in working lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the tooth is stuck and hard, it is necessary to drill around it, as you administer cuts with tapers, not piercing beyond the tooth's root, and it should have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the tooth;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you should have several, so that each time it comes back into its place from the edge of the bone, so that you have marks for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three ways of marking:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one mark on the bone, and turn your fingers to both sides until you feel that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the mark on another part of the bone slightly later, and thus do all around, then cut the distance between the bones of the bone that is between the joints, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take the bone in your hand, or any of the tools you have such as pliers, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is advisable to reset the open part that remains of the bone with all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if nothing remains of the small bones or scales, do not remove them lightly with any instrument.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with bandages and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of work is this one that the Gauls describe, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the pain is very strong, and that is its word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must remove a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you can insert the lens-shaped piece of this surgical instrument into it:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one part, and it is the affected part in the second rib, so that the cutter is towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly cut the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is outside.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, then lightly cut the bone, because one should not cut harmfully or without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone's fracture does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only broken from above, and there are small pieces, then you should smooth out that roughness, and remove the scales with the delicate scraper that you should have various quantities of, to manage each limb according to its convenience, following the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use great scrapers first, and then more delicate ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-splitting and delicate cuts, it is necessary that you mitigate according to its advancement.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that cannot be answered by one who has studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is discovered, then it is necessary to take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another piece of cloth doubled in two or three, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first piece of cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more gently than you can, so as not to aggravate the wound, then administer by pouring over another piece of cloth, and do not strain it unless it stains the wound only.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it remain there for one or two days until the abscess is soothed, then dislodge it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, wheat flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make powders from these things, and put on the wound, and administer medicines such as mustard, without causing irritation;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is kept clean, do not leave any pus, and do not allow any pus to collect, for when pus collects on the brain's surface, it causes great harm;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when one places a sharp object above the wound, do not prick it from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take precaution then, for if no accidents come to the patient, as we have said, it is uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no other remedy comes to hand except the one you have placed above it, then it is necessary that you apply a piece of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one cloth, and put it on top of the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the appropriate methods of treatment until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Be careful not to break both parts of the nose above, or one by itself, as there are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And that one is cartilaginous and does not break easily, so it does not cause deformity or twisting, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	If one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you bend your little finger or thumb into the break in your index finger, and set it inside the break until the finger regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, so that the pain does not increase because of your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nail, and cannot reach the finger to the bone, then it is necessary that you place it inside the head of a pin or needle, slightly larger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, do the other side as well, and hurry to restore the first joint if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the swelling of the abscess has subsided, then bend the tip of the finger towards the palm of the hand with pieces of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you put another bone, if the fracture is there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and they are so large that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said no restorer should moisten the tents in the morning, and kill each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it should be ground in the making of an ointment with egg yolk and flour;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the bone, until the bone is iron and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never use goose feathers in place of bones, and if the sore is wrapped, and the fracture is held, and blows the pain away.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working, put cotton or milled cloth soaked in red oil or a drop of iodine into it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if there are no abscesses, put on plaster made from mustard flour and powdered incense, mixed with honey, then place light bandages, and do not tie the nose tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the broken piece of the nose is small and in many pieces, then extract them with suitable instruments, then clean the wound, and care for the injured parts with charcoal and sutures, as appropriate for plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound in the nose, then treat with tents and apply cold compresses until healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured, and there is no wound elsewhere, and the fracture is only slight, and not completely broken into two pieces, because of the teeth inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, to break your right index finger in the patient's mouth.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is in the left mandible, break your right index finger with the right hand, and gently break the fracture inside, and fix it with the other hand by default, and make even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is in two parts, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movements of the teeth occur, or breakage, then strain with a gold or silver or silk thread, then place above the broken jaw, and place on the double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place on the cloth a well-made large stick, or a piece of leather even and long according to the mandible, and tie it above the mouth that you can, and command the patient to rest, and feed him light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the position changes, then release it to the animal, and then put it back as it was changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And place a poultice on top, of powder from the mill with plenty of honey or flour of mustard, after you have removed the crust.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And place another light poultice on top, and if the poultice becomes hard, and the position of the patient does not change, leave it until he is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come to the face, then follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, do not apply any piece of the bone that is broken.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If it is applied too closely to the skin, it may cause infection.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, then expand it according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have removed all these pieces, and there is no delay, if the wound is wide, and it has been cleaned, then apply ointments to it, to draw out pus until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the bandage
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forearm breaks several times before, behind the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and displaced in two, and there are pieces, and it is the least heavy to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is fracture with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is that if the fracture is near the wound, you should have two assistants, so that one can hold the injured forearm that is broken;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the others stretch the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then make the fracture even at both ends, so that it forms as it should, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have the skill to extend further, place a rounded, flat cloth or linen ball on the shoulder, as large as your need.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and pull the lever, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you make the fracture even as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the shoulder of the arm from behind, because it comes out in front, then it is necessary that the hairs of the armpit be pulled evenly over their surface, and the assistant holds the shoulder back, and pushes the shoulder down, until the bone of the arm is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then bring the fracture together at both ends, and if the bones are broken, it is necessary to cut through.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and get light pieces, and if the bone cannot join for any reason, then use one of the knives you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but put the forceps on this instrument to hold the gum:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it looks like a spoon, and is not fixed, and should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the work:
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should have two prongs, like you see, and one wide and the other narrow, as is the edge of the wound that you made when you cut the bones:
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of the abscess, cut the wound, and if the edge is small, or you doubt the abscess, then fill the wound with bandages and poultices according to its amount.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if it is an abscess that comes, then soak the bandage in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The setting of a bone, when it is in pain and when it is cut, is that you place above the bone the plaster from the mill powder and some egg, and put light dressings on, and place a sphere outside the wound, if you have skill.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large bandage of a palm's width, then place the cloth double above the dressings and the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin splint of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the head of the bandage hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the splint on the fractured part, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and outside the wound, healthy and unhealthy.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the bone is broken evenly, and you clearly see that the dislocated joint does not move over the broken bone, reward it every day, and when the bones are aligned, hold them in place.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the dislocated joint rest on its back, and place the small splint below the joint to lift the dislocation up.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if the broken bone aligns with the shoulder alignment, or you tie the arm to the neck, and it does not dislocate for 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then reapply the plaster if you see that there is a need for it, and hold it in place until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored within 28 days, and less to some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	There are cases where the shoulder is broken or dislocated in the middle of the arm, and it does not stay in place except by touch.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the splint according to the shape of the fracture, and the limb is realigned according to its natural form, in all ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then apply the powder from the mill with an abundance of urine, and light bandages, and put it on top of the bandage.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then place a wide and thin spatula, slightly larger than the shoulder span, under the shoulder, and if it does not hold in any part of the shoulder, use a cloth of linen to support it evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then hold it firmly with a great bend, so that the spatula does not move from its place, and watch the joint each day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it collapses, hold it firmly and if it is out of its place, support it evenly and grind the hairs on its ribs.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is completed, if it dislocates, and you are sure, for it is not bone that can be put back forcefully.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is sticking out before, and not completely outside, then cut it off, and the bone, and do as we have said in the fracture of the forearm to alleviate an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the pinky
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The pain is never broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the back.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends outwards, and the patient feels great pain, and loss of all function, and possibly vomiting blood, and open the veins in the broken bone, and the patient feels well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the hairs grow out over their back, and the arrowhead is placed between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulders, and gather the ribs of both sides in your hands, and subtly put it back in all the ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place bandages and swabs above the thin skin of salt, or another light one, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And turn the bandage around the back, and tighten it evenly, and rub the wound every hour, and if it dislocates again, tighten it.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	And if it is necessary to release it, for corrosion or for itching that comes to the limb, or pain or abscess, then hurry and release it, and change the bandage, and apply what has come from various methods of treatment.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the splint, and hold it steady until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	That the rib fracturer comes only from great force after the back, and at the top of the chest, and does not fracture for any other reason than that they are brittle.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and the pain is felt at the inquiry as it should be.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and the bandage with a splint if you know how to do it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture is inclined inward, it feels great pain and tenderness, as if of a wound, because the ribs do not knit together.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and there is a gap, and all the rest is filled with great blood, and it is a difficult healing, and the ancients had much concern.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it should be administered foods that cause the stomach to swell, to push the broken bone out of place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	Let us not do this, unless there is a case where it does not come, if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said of those who put suction cups on the limb, to draw out formally, and this is similar to reason;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Nevertheless, doubt and the fact that the suction cup does not draw out the excess from the limb due to its weak position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that none of those who should cover the limb with wool smeared in oil high, and put tents between the ribs to equal the liquid inside, then heal the care of pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the limb pains greatly that it cannot bear the weight of the bone which points to the sling, and doubt is at the limb, then it is necessary to cut across the limb from the broken side, and it is necessary to place a restraining instrument for the wound.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must drill the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat with ointments, until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if abscesses come out, put soft cloths soaked in red oil on the wound;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the wound as it is necessary for the abscess, and let it lie flat on the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Never does a fracture of the neck bones come, and very little when it does rain;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you see whether they will be healthy or not, if you take note if their hands are softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or extend, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is often fatal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when you hold them and not, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the pains are healed, if you put care.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, take note whether the feet are soft, and if the accidents that are in hand are present, and there is movement on the back and egestion without volition;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when placed on their back, they void involuntarily.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it lies on its back and wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	It is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if not treated properly.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to them, it is the lighter of the two.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you should rub it with red wine or egg yolk oil until it is calmed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that side where they feel the pain until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone is dislocated, it must be covered with a bandage;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and break the bone, then gather the two edges of the wound, if it is large, at a seam, then apply the healing ointment with charcoal, as long as they are clean.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the bone is broken, which is called the "bone of the elbow", then take your right hand and place it on the other hand at your wrist, then apply the plaster and the bandage above, if you have the skill.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then strap it, and if there is bone decay, then above, and the bone, and heal the wound until it is clean.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ribs of the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It rarely happens that the ribs of the back are broken, and if it does, it is not from a slight blow to the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and if they are broken, they extend long and decline to the spine, causing great pain, swelling, and bruising at the site of the break.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over, as high as you can above the broken rib;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and carefully examine where the break and the shape of the bone are.
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the break is only at the top, then align it with the natural shape of the bone.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long and it declines inwards, place the limb above its belly until the restoration of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have put it back in place, apply the ointment, then apply a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the broken part still so it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and place the limb outside the ribs, until the joint is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their sound side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if it swells and hurts, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed, and apply what we have already said.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then proceed with the treatment, and hold it in place as necessary, unless there is no bad consequence.
et c’est li maniere.	And that is how to do it.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The assistants are those located between the neck and the shoulder blade, and if they are broken, one should restore them according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one is that you take a single thick needle, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	and tie the two ends together, and let them rise up, and cut the painful part above the seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then pour the broken arm over the needle, until it reaches ease, and has half an inch of needle, then let it go over any heavy thing or the nurse extends it down;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then put the broken piece of bone together with your hands, until the broken piece returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one pricks the sore above its base, and places the hand on his collar, then commands two ministers to prick the vein that is above the breaker at his hands, and the others prick everywhere around it, and stretches each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, then hold the eye away from the breaker, above the breaker, and stretch each of the ministers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fractured bone is close to the top of the shoulder, it is necessary to put a median line of splints on one side of the shoulder, and the other towards the back, away from the fracture.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	Similarly, if the fractured bone is towards the back, it is necessary to put a light line of splints slightly downwards until the fracture is aligned with the shoulder and the back.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then align the fracture as it should be, and hold it steady, if there are no abscesses that come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if there are abscesses that come, do not hold it steady for the next seven days, and put on a soft bandage in oil and rosemary, until the abscess is soothed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then the strain, and the method of straining is that you place the splint on the fractured part, then bring the arm up with the aid, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the bandage, and strain with the aid, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and place on the fracture a stronger and wider splint than the others, and have between each splint two inches of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers from each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then strain them over the stones, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less when moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the sitting of the stones and the pressure, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess is healed, leave it to lie for seven days, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look at each three days the joint, that the itching does not spread and come to the limb, or the inflammations do not come to the limb because it is too stiff.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents occur, it should not be removed until after three days or more, and the pain should lie on his back, and he should have his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and apply a bandage to the dislocation in a plain cloth equally, and look every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken member does not move, or that the tendons are not softened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if the pain is reduced by the power of medicine, and give him the meat that we have put before, in such a way that the meat is at the first subtle;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to eat again, it should be soft.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be reset within 40 days of the injury.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And then one should apply poultices and give baths to the limb to promote healing.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If its structure is crooked and swollen, it may take forty days or two months to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, called the "humerus", one of which is smaller and is the one that forms the elbow joint.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	And the other is large and is the one that is outside, next to the small one.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Possibly the larger humerus or the smaller one is broken alone, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the smaller humerus is broken, the recovery and healing are easy.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the large bones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If the small bones are broken alone, then it is best to slightly extend and align them.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is a large fracture, then it must be pulled more forcefully.
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	And extend it up to the cushion of the hand, and the small fingers higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and the thumbs cross over themselves, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the fingers do not suffer any labor.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the ministers of the arm to the part outside of his hand, or to the elbow, and others to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mirror evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is no need to hold the bone in place, and you cannot restore it to its original position, then do as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the bone breaker there is a wound, I have spoken about it to the chapter scribe;
si pren la cure.	if you take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses, then glue the cloth of a poultice made of rose oil and white wax, which is not too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and tie the cloth by lifting it slightly, until the abscesses are relieved.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	Then remove the poultice, and put on the plaster of the powder from the mill with abundant honey, then place the splints, and let the splint of the bone breaker stick out more, and a little wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and make sure he has six or more arms in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracturer is in one of the bones or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and holds it above the fracturer and keeps pulling, as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the cloths that are on the fracturer be soft and moist, and not too hard or sharp;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread that is being pulled be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the member and the limb after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should raise the limb in hot water, until those itches are calmed;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	Let the limb remain at ease and not be constricted.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then continue the strapping, and if the joint is dislocated and the bones are displaced, similarly, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the tendons cannot come to the member, because it is too tight, then you must slacken it slightly, and let it rest for some time, until the tendons are corrected, and then strap it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If none of these things we have said come to harm, it will not be necessary to look at them for twenty years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or ask them to lean back, then place their hands on their neck, and keep their neck even, and avoid movement and disturbance, and sleep on their back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And wash that fracture in 30 days or 50 days, and perhaps in 20 days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the breakage of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Then let it be at the back of the hand and we have few breakages, and only bleeding many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the bone of the hand is broken or crushed, it is necessary that the hairs be cut short and evenly, and be straight in front of him equally.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then place his hand on the extended board, and extend the bones that are broken, and put them evenly in the bones, until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	And apply the plaster and cloths, if there are no abscesses, then put an ointment according to the amount of the limb.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fractured bone is in the arch of the foot, then make a roll of cloth, and instruct the patient to bend it against his broken foot.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then strain it with a long cloth, and let the ointment be as large as the sole of the hand, and apply it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, it is necessary to place a splint above and another below the wrist, so that the hand is open and straight, then wrap the entire arm around the hand, and bind the injured part between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fractured bone comes to any of the above joints, if it is the wrist, then put it evenly, as needed.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and hold it with a plant, and if you see that you put a straight small stake to lift the broken piece, and do not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the broken piece is like the others, such as in the index or another one, if it is aligned, and tie it with the healthy joint that comes after.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you tie them all by holding them, as long as they are worth, or you put a stake on top, such as a pouch.
